            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Tyler Collins is a lefty power bat with 20 homer potential if he gets enough at-bats with the Tigers. Ideally he will find balance between his power stroke and previous batting average history. Steven Moya is another lefty power bat with more batting average on balls in play potential coming from his own power and speed combination. Detroit's backup corner outfield situation could wind up being a fun competition yielding fantasy-relevant results from one of Collins or Moya if there's an injury to a starter or J.D. Martinez regresses hard core. Keep an eye on their balls in play breakdown and batted ball spray, as well as their playing time in the spring. If Collins goes full out power stroke and/or gets pull-happy, the batting average will suffer.  (<a href="https://twitter.com/RotoBanter">Dan Schwartz</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The decision between Tyler Collins and Steven Moya won't have to come this year, since the Tigers have veteran options in left and right field. But the decision will come soon, and it will have fantasy relevance either way.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Collins is one of those fringe prospects who benefited by being in the Tigers' system. Given that it is almost always thin, Collins lingered around the top 10 even though he wouldn't have made the lists of many other clubs. Not all top 10s are created equally of course, but when you consistently see a name, you end up giving him a modicum of value in the fantasy market, especially in deeper leagues where the name-recognition almost sells him more than anything. Anyway, the point is he's a fourth outfielder. He actually didn't have a huge platoon split in the minors with a capable .767 OPS against lefties (but a blah .781 v. righties). There's a little punch, a little speed, and a decent batting average floor because he doesn't strike out like crazy. (Paul Sporer)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Collins has dropped his minor league OPS every single season, including a .662 in 218 plate appearances at Triple-A last year, though he ended up holding his own in the majors in a near-equal sample (.732 in 207). The lefty outfielder has a real fourth-outfielder feel to his game, but he could get a chance to work the strong side of the platoon.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>At various points throughout the minors, Tyler Collins flashed a little bit of everything. His 18-homer, 12-steal, .263 campaign in Triple-A in 2014 exemplifies the close-but-not-quite offensive profile a fantasy owner might use to justify a sleeper pick. At 26, though, the speed has already waned, and the power is modest at best - certainly not enough to justify a .250 average and .300 OBP. He's a perfectly average major league hitter, making him a decidedly inadequate fantasy asset. It doesn't mean he couldn't contribute in a platoon for an AL-only league, which is precisely what he figures to do as the strong side of the Tigers' center field platoon. There's just not much upside here, so any reliance on Collins should be done strategically (i.e. only against righties in deeper formats). (Alex Chamberlain)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Collins is the personification of the league-average batting line, which makes for a decent real baseball player but a lackluster fantasy asset. He could generate value when used strategically in a platoon in AL-only leagues, but he will otherwise bear little fruit.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
